Task instruction sent to agent 
# Task: Implement CompactDiffFormatter for Terraform

## Objective
Create a `CompactDiffFormatter` in `internal/command/format/` that produces a condensed,
summary-style diff output for `terraform plan`, showing only resource-level changes
without attribute-level detail.

## Requirements

1. **Create `internal/command/format/compact.go`** with:
   - `CompactDiffFormatter` struct implementing a plan formatter
   - `Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *terraform.Schemas)` method returning string
   - Outputs one line per resource change: `[action] resource_type.name`
   - Groups changes by action type (create/update/delete/replace)
   - Shows summary counts at the end

2. **Create `internal/command/format/compact_test.go`** with tests

3. **Follow Terraform patterns**:
   - Study the existing `DiffFormatter` in the format package
   - Use `plans.Action` constants (Create, Update, Delete, etc.)
   - Use `addrs.AbsResourceInstance` for resource addressing

## Key Reference Files
- `internal/command/format/diff.go` — existing diff formatter
- `internal/command/format/state.go` — state formatter pattern
- `internal/plans/changes.go` — plan change types
- `internal/plans/plan.go` — Plan struct definition
- `internal/addrs/resource.go` — resource addressing

## Success Criteria
- CompactDiffFormatter struct exists in format package
- Format method accepts plan and schemas parameters
- Outputs resource-level change summary
- Groups by action type
- Test file exists

     4→// Package format contains helpers for formatting various Terraform
     5→// structures for human-readabout output.
     6→//
     7→// This package is used by the official Terraform CLI in formatting any
     8→// output and is exported to encourage non-official frontends to mimic the
     9→// output formatting as much as possible so that text formats of Terraform
    10→// structures have a consistent look and feel.
    11→package format
    12→
    13→import "github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"
    14→
    15→// DiffActionSymbol returns a string that, once passed through a
    16→// colorstring.Colorize, will produce a result that can be written
    17→// to a terminal to produce a symbol made of three printable
    18→// characters, possibly interspersed with VT100 color codes.
    19→func DiffActionSymbol(action plans.Action) string {
    20→	switch action {
    21→	case plans.DeleteThenCreate:
    22→		return "[red]-[reset]/[green]+[reset]"
    23→	case plans.CreateThenDelete:
    24→		return "[green]+[reset]/[red]-[reset]"
    25→	case plans.Create:
    26→		return "  [green]+[reset]"
    27→	case plans.Delete:
    28→		return "  [red]-[reset]"
    29→	case plans.Forget:
    30→		return " [red].[reset]"
    31→	case plans.CreateThenForget:
    32→		return " [green]+[reset]/[red].[reset]"
    33→	case plans.Read:
    34→		return " [cyan]<=[reset]"
    35→	case plans.Update:
    36→		return "  [yellow]~[reset]"
    37→	case plans.NoOp:
    38→		return "   "
    39→	default:
    40→		return "  ?"
    41→	}
    42→}
    43→

     4→package plans
     5→
     6→type Action rune
     7→
     8→const (
     9→	NoOp             Action = 0
    10→	Create           Action = '+'
    11→	Read             Action = '←'
    12→	Update           Action = '~'
    13→	DeleteThenCreate Action = '∓'
    14→	CreateThenDelete Action = '±'
    15→	Delete           Action = '-'
    16→	Forget           Action = '.'
    17→	CreateThenForget Action = '⨥'
    18→	Open             Action = '⟃'
    19→	Renew            Action = '⟳'
    20→	Close            Action = '⫏'
    21→)
    22→
    23→//go:generate go tool golang.org/x/tools/cmd/stringer -type Action
    24→
    25→// IsReplace returns true if the action is one of the actions that
    26→// represent replacing an existing object with a new object.
    27→func (a Action) IsReplace() bool {
    28→	return a == DeleteThenCreate || a == CreateThenDelete || a == CreateThenForget
    29→}

   232→type ResourceInstanceChangeSrc struct {
   233→	// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change
   234→	// will apply to.
   235→	//
   236→	// THIS IS NOT A SUFFICIENT UNIQUE IDENTIFIER! It doesn't consider the
   237→	// fact that multiple objects for the same resource instance might be
   238→	// present in the same plan; use the ObjectAddr method instead if you
   239→	// need a unique address for a particular change.
   240→	Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance
   241→
   242→	// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the
   243→	// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the
   244→	// current object.
   245→	//
   246→	// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will
   247→	// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement. In that case,
   248→	// DeposedKey in the plan is always states.NotDeposed, representing that
   249→	// the current object is being replaced with the deposed.
   250→	DeposedKey states.DeposedKey
   251→
   252→	// PrevRunAddr is the absolute address that this resource instance had at
   253→	// the conclusion of a previous run.
   254→	//
   255→	// This will typically be the same as Addr, but can be different if the
   256→	// previous resource instance was subject to a "moved" block that we
   257→	// handled in the process of creating this plan.
   258→	//
   259→	// For the initial creation of a resource instance there isn't really any
   260→	// meaningful "previous run address", but PrevRunAddr will still be set
   261→	// equal to Addr in that case in order to simplify logic elsewhere which
   262→	// aims to detect and react to the movement of instances between addresses.
   263→	PrevRunAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance
   264→

   467→type ChangeSrc struct {
   468→	// Action defines what kind of change is being made.
   469→	Action Action
   470→
   471→	// Before and After correspond to the fields of the same name in Change,
   472→	// but have not yet been decoded from the serialized value used for
   473→	// storage.
   474→	Before, After DynamicValue
   475→
   476→	// BeforeIdentity and AfterIdentity correspond to the fields of the same name in Change,
   477→	// but have not yet been decoded from the serialized value used for
   478→	// storage.
   479→	BeforeIdentity, AfterIdentity DynamicValue
   480→
   481→	// BeforeSensitivePaths and AfterSensitivePaths are the paths for any
   482→	// values in Before or After (respectively) that are considered to be
   483→	// sensitive. The sensitive marks are removed from the in-memory values
   484→	// to enable encoding (marked values cannot be marshalled), and so we
   485→	// store the sensitive paths to allow re-marking later when we decode
   486→	// the serialized change.
   487→	BeforeSensitivePaths, AfterSensitivePaths []cty.Path
   488→
   489→	// Importing is present if the resource is being imported as part of this
   490→	// change.
   491→	//
   492→	// Use the simple presence of this field to detect if a ChangeSrc is to be
   493→	// imported, the contents of this structure may be modified going forward.
   494→	Importing *ImportingSrc
   495→
   496→	// GeneratedConfig contains any HCL config generated for this resource

    11→
    12→// Schemas is a container for various kinds of schema that Terraform needs
    13→// during processing.
    14→type Schemas struct {
    15→	Providers    map[addrs.Provider]providers.ProviderSchema
    16→	Provisioners map[string]*configschema.Block
    17→}
    18→
    19→// ProviderSchema returns the entire ProviderSchema object that was produced
    20→// by the plugin for the given provider, or nil if no such schema is available.
    21→//
    22→// It's usually better to go use the more precise methods offered by type
    23→// Schemas to handle this detail automatically.
    24→func (ss *Schemas) ProviderSchema(provider addrs.Provider) providers.ProviderSchema {
    25→	return ss.Providers[provider]
    26→}
    27→
    28→// ProviderConfig returns the schema for the provider configuration of the
    29→// given provider type, or nil if no such schema is available.
    30→func (ss *Schemas) ProviderConfig(provider addrs.Provider) *configschema.Block {
    31→	return ss.ProviderSchema(provider).Provider.Body
    32→}
    33→
    34→// ResourceTypeConfig returns the schema for the configuration of a given
    35→// resource type belonging to a given provider type, or an empty schema
    36→// if no such schema is available.
    37→//
    38→// In many cases the provider type is inferrable from the resource type name,
    39→// but this is not always true because users can override the provider for
    40→// a resource 
... (truncated)

     1→# generate runs `go generate` to build the dynamically generated
     2→# source files, except the protobuf stubs which are built instead with
     3→# "make protobuf".
     4→generate:
     5→	go generate ./...
     6→
     7→# We separate the protobuf generation because most development tasks on
     8→# Terraform do not involve changing protobuf files and protoc is not a
     9→# go-gettable dependency and so getting it installed can be inconvenient.
    10→#
    11→# If you are working on changes to protobuf interfaces, run this Makefile
    12→# target to be sure to regenerate all of the protobuf stubs using the expected
    13→# versions of protoc and the protoc Go plugins.
    14→protobuf:
    15→	go run ./tools/protobuf-compile .
    16→
    17→fmtcheck:
    18→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/gofmtcheck.sh"
    19→
    20→importscheck:
    21→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/goimportscheck.sh"
    22→
    23→vetcheck:
    24→	@echo "==> Checking that the code complies with go vet requirements"
    25→	@go vet ./...
    26→
    27→staticcheck:
    28→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/staticcheck.sh"
    29→
    30→exhaustive:
    31→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/exhaustive.sh"
    32→
    33→copyright:
    34→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/copyright.sh" --plan
    35→
    36→copyrightfix:
    37→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/copyright.sh"
    38→
    39→syncdeps:
    40→	"$(CURDIR)/scripts/syncdeps.sh"
    41→
    42→# disallow any parallelism (-j) for Make. This is necessary since some
    43→# commands during the build process create temporary files that collide
    44→# under parallel conditions.
    45→.NOTPARALLEL:
    46→
    47→.PHONY: fmtcheck importscheck vetcheck generate protobuf staticcheck syncdeps
    48→

# Simplify: Code Review and Cleanup

Review all changed files for reuse, quality, and efficiency. Fix any issues found.

## Phase 1: Identify Changes

Run `git diff` (or `git diff HEAD` if there are staged changes) to see what changed. If there are no git changes, review the most recently modified files that the user mentioned or that you edited earlier in this conversation.

## Phase 2: Launch Three Review Agents in Parallel

Use the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.

### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review

For each change:

1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.
2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.
3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.

### Agent 2: Code Quality Review

Review the same changes for hacky patterns:

1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls
2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones
3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction
4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries
5. **Stringly-type

Look for:
1. Unnecessary work (redundant computations, repeated operations)
2. Missed concurrency (independent operations that could run in parallel)

    14→)
    15→
    16→// CompactDiffFormatter is a plan formatter that produces a condensed,
    17→// summary-style diff output showing only resource-level changes
    18→// without attribute-level detail.
    19→type CompactDiffFormatter struct{}
    20→
    21→// Format produces a compact, summary-style diff output for a plan.
    22→// It shows one line per resource change: [action] resource_type.name
    23→// Groups changes by action type and shows summary counts at the end.
    24→func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
    25→	var buf bytes.Buffer
    26→
    27→	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {
    28→		return ""
    29→	}
    30→
    31→	// Group resources by action
    32→	changes := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)
    33→	for _, resource := range plan.Changes.Resources {
    34→		if resource == nil {
    35→			continue
    36→		}
    37→		// Skip NoOp actions unless we need to show them
    38→		if resource.Action != plans.NoOp {
    39→			changes[resource.Action] = append(changes[resource.Action], resource)
    40→		}
    41→	}
    42→
    43→	// Define the order to display action types
    44→	actionOrder := []plans.Action{
    45→		plans.Create,
    46→		plans.Update,
    47→		plans.Delete,
    48→		plans.DeleteThenCreate,
    49→		plans.CreateThenDelete,
    50→		plans.Read,
    51→		plans.Forget,
    52→		pl
... (truncated)

    11→// ObjectValueID takes a value that is assumed to be an object representation
    12→// of some resource instance object and attempts to heuristically find an
    13→// attribute of it that is likely to be a unique identifier in the remote
    14→// system that it belongs to which will be useful to the user.
    15→//
    16→// If such an attribute is found, its name and string value intended for
    17→// display are returned. Both returned strings are empty if no such attribute
    18→// exists, in which case the caller should assume that the resource instance
    19→// address within the Terraform configuration is the best available identifier.
    20→//
    21→// This is only a best-effort sort of thing, relying on naming conventions in
    22→// our resource type schemas. The result is not guaranteed to be unique, but
    23→// should generally be suitable for display to an end-user anyway.
    24→//
    25→// This function will panic if the given value is not of an object type.
    26→func ObjectValueID(obj cty.Value) (k, v string) {
    27→	if obj.IsNull() || !obj.IsKnown() {
    28→		return "", ""
    29→	}
    30→
    31→	atys := obj.Type().AttributeTypes()
    32→
    33→	switch {
    34→
    35→	case atys["id"] == cty.String:
    36→		v := obj.GetAttr("id")
    37→		if marks.Has(v, marks.Sensitive) {
    38→			break
    39→		}
    40→		v, _ = v.Unmark()
    41→
    42→		if v.IsKnown() && !v.IsNull() {
    43→			return "id", v.AsString()
    44→		}
    45→
    46→	case atys["name"] == cty.String:

     1→// Copyright IBM Corp. 2014, 2026

     4→// Package format contains helpers for formatting various Terraform
     5→// structures for human-readabout output.
     6→//
     7→// This package is used by the official Terraform CLI in formatting any
     8→// output and is exported to encourage non-official frontends to mimic the
     9→// output formatting as much as possible so that text formats of Terraform
    10→// structures have a consistent look and feel.
    11→package format
    12→
    13→import "github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"
    14→
    15→// DiffActionSymbol returns a string that, once passed through a
    16→// colorstring.Colorize, will produce a result that can be written
    17→// to a terminal to produce a symbol made of three printable
    18→// characters, possibly interspersed with VT100 color codes.
    19→func DiffActionSymbol(action plans.Action) string {
    20→	switch action {
    21→	case plans.DeleteThenCreate:
    22→		return "[red]-[reset]/[green]+[reset]"
    23→	case plans.CreateThenDelete:
    24→		return "[green]+[reset]/[red]-[reset]"
    25→	case plans.Create:
    26→		return "  [green]+[reset]"
    27→	case plans.Delete:
    28→		return "  [red]-[reset]"
    29→	case plans.Forget:
    30→		return " [red].[reset]"
    31→	case plans.CreateThenForget:
    32→		return " [green]+[reset]/[red].[reset]"
    33→	case plans.Read:
    34→		return " [cyan]<=[reset]"
    35→	case plans.Update:
    36→		return "  [yellow]~[reset]"
    37→	case plans.NoOp:
    38→		return "   "
    39→	default:
    40→		return "  ?"
    41→	}
    42→}
    43→

    25→// IsReplace returns true if the action is one of the actions that
    26→// represent replacing an existing object with a new object.

    14→
    15→// DiffActionSymbol returns a string that, once passed through a
    16→// colorstring.Colorize, will produce a result that can be written
    17→// to a terminal to produce a symbol made of three printable
    18→// characters, possibly interspersed with VT100 color codes.
    19→func DiffActionSymbol(action plans.Action) string {
    20→	switch action {
    21→	case plans.DeleteThenCreate:
    22→		return "[red]-[reset]/[green]+[reset]"
    23→	case plans.CreateThenDelete:
    24→		return "[green]+[reset]/[red]-[reset]"
    25→	case plans.Create:
    26→		return "  [green]+[reset]"
    27→	case plans.Delete:
    28→		return "  [red]-[reset]"
    29→	case plans.Forget:
    30→		return " [red].[reset]"
    31→	case plans.CreateThenForget:
    32→		return " [green]+[reset]/[red].[reset]"
    33→	case plans.Read:
    34→		return " [cyan]<=[reset]"
    35→	case plans.Update:
    36→		return "  [yellow]~[reset]"
    37→	case plans.NoOp:
    38→		return "   "
    39→	default:
    40→		return "  ?"
    41→	}
    42→}
    43→

     1→// Copyright IBM Corp. 2014, 2026
     2→// SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1
     3→
     4→package format
     5→
     6→import (
     7→	"strings"
     8→
     9→	"github.com/mitchellh/colorstring"
    10→	wordwrap "github.com/mitchellh/go-wordwrap"
    11→)
    12→
    13→// HorizontalRule returns a newline character followed by a number of
    14→// horizontal line characters to fill the given width.
    15→//
    16→// If the given colorize has colors enabled, the rule will also be given a
    17→// dark grey color to attempt to visually de-emphasize it for sighted users.
    18→//
    19→// This is intended for printing to the UI via hashicorp/cli.UI.Output, or
    20→// similar, which will automatically append a trailing newline too.
    21→func HorizontalRule(color *colorstring.Colorize, width int) string {
    22→	if width <= 1 {
    23→		return "\n"
    24→	}
    25→	rule := strings.Repeat("─", width-1)
    26→	if color == nil { // sometimes unit tests don't populate this properly
    27→		return "\n" + rule
    28→	}
    29→	return color.Color("[dark_gray]\n" + rule)
    30→}
    31→
    32→// WordWrap takes a string containing unbroken lines of text and inserts
    33→// newline characters to try to make the text fit within the given width.
    34→//
    35→// The string can already contain newline characters, for example if you are
    36→// trying to render multiple paragraphs of text. (In that case, our usual
    37→// style would be to have _two_ newline characters as the paragraph separator.)
    38→//
    39→// As a special case, any line that begins with at least one space will be left
    40→// unbroken. This allows including literal segments in the output, such as
    41→// code snippets or filenames, where word wrapping would be confusing.

... (truncated)

func actionString(action string) []string {
	switch {
	case action == "NoOp":
		return []string{"no-op"}
	case action == "Create":
		return []string{"create"}
	case action == "Delete":
		return []string{"delete"}
	case action == "Update":
		return []string{"update"}
	case action == "CreateThenDelete":
		return []string{"create", "delete"}
	case action == "Read":
		return []string{"read"}
	case action == "DeleteThenCreate":
		return []string{"delete", "create"}
	case action == "Forget":
		return []string{"forget"}
	case action == "CreateThenForget":
		return []string{"create", "forget"}
	default:
		return []string{action}
	}
}

// UnmarshalActions reverses the actionString function.
func UnmarshalActions(actions []string) plans.Action {
	if len(actions) == 2 {
		if actions[0] == "create" && actions[1] == "delete" {
			return plans.CreateThenDelete
		}

Now let me create a comprehensive efficiency report based on my analysis of the CompactDiffFormatter implementation:

## Efficiency Analysis Report: CompactDiffFormatter

I've reviewed `/workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go` and identified several efficiency issues:

### **1. CRITICAL: Inefficient Summary String Building (Lines 141-148)**

**Issue:** Classic string concatenation in a loop causing repeated allocations
```go
summary := ""
for i, item := range summaryItems {
    if i == 0 {
        summary = item
    } else {
        summary += ", " + item  // ← Each iteration allocates new string
    }
}
```

**Impact:** With N items, this creates O(N) string allocations. For a summary with 7-8 items, creates 6+ unnecessary allocations.

**Recommendation:** Use `strings.Join()` instead:
```go
summary := strings.Join(summaryItems, ", ")
```

---

### **2. MAJOR: Unnecessary actionStrings Map Pre-allocation (Lines 57-65)**

**Issue:** A hardcoded map with all possible Action values is populated regardless of which actions are actually in the plan.
```go
actionStrings := make(map[plans.Action]string)
actionStrings[plans.Create] = "create"
actionStrings[plans.Update] = "update"
// ... 5 more entries, all unconditionally populated
```

**Impact:** Creates a 8-entry map on every Format() call, even if the plan only contains 1-2 action types. Wasted memory and initialization work.

**Recommendation:** Use a constant map or lazy initialization only for actions present in `changes`.

---

### **3. MAJOR: Inefficient Summary Building Logic (Lines 102-138)**

**Issue:** Explicit handling of each action type with separate count variables and conditionals
```go

    94→func (v *OperationHuman) Plan(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *terraform.Schemas) {

    96→	if err != nil {
    97→		v.view.streams.Eprintf("Failed to marshal plan to json: %s", err)
    98→		return
    99→	}
   100→
   101→	renderer := jsonformat.Renderer{
   102→		Colorize:            v.view.colorize,
   103→		Streams:             v.view.streams,
   104→		RunningInAutomation: v.inAutomation,
   105→	}
   106→
   107→	jplan := jsonformat.Plan{
   108→		PlanFormatVersion:     jsonplan.FormatVersion,
   109→		ProviderFormatVersion: jsonprovider.FormatVersion,
   110→		OutputChanges:         outputs,
   111→		ResourceChanges:       changed,
   112→		ResourceDrift:         drift,
   113→		ProviderSchemas:       jsonprovider.MarshalForRenderer(schemas),
   114→		RelevantAttributes:    attrs,
   115→		ActionInvocations:     actions,
   116→	}
   117→
   118→	// Side load some data that we can't extract from the JSON plan.
   119→	var opts []plans.Quality
   120→	if plan.Errored {
   121→		opts = append(opts, plans.Errored)
   122→	} else if !plan.Applyable {
   123→		// FIXME: There might be other reasons for "non-applyable" in future,
   124→		// so maybe we should check plan.Changes.IsEmpty here and use a more
   125→		// generic fallback message if the plan doesn't seem to be empty.
   126→		// There are currently no other cases though, so we'll keep it
   127→		// simple for now.
   128→		opts = append(opts, plans.NoChanges)
   129→	}
   130→
   131→	renderer.RenderHumanPlan(jplan, plan.UIMode, opts...)
   132→}

func actionDescription(action plans.Action) string {
	switch action {
	case plans.Create:
		return "  [green]+[reset] create"
	case plans.Delete:
		return "  [red]-[reset] destroy"
	case plans.Update:
		return "  [yellow]~[reset] update in-place"
	case plans.CreateThenDelete:
		return "[green]+[reset]/[red]-[reset] create replacement and then destroy"
	case plans.DeleteThenCreate:
		return "[red]-[reset]/[green]+[reset] destroy and then create replacement"
	case plans.Read:
		return " [cyan]<=[reset] read (data resources)"
	default:
		panic(fmt.Sprintf("unrecognized change type: %s", action.String()))
	}
}

## Code Quality Review: CompactDiffFormatter

Based on my analysis of `/workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go`, I've identified several code quality issues:

### 1. **Stringly-Typed Code - Hardcoded Action String Mappings** (CRITICAL)

**Issue**: Lines 57-65 manually map `plans.Action` constants to human-readable strings:
```go
actionStrings := make(map[plans.Action]string)
actionStrings[plans.Create] = "create"
actionStrings[plans.Update] = "update"
// ... etc
```

**Problem**: 
- The `plans.Action` type already has a generated `String()` method (in `/workspace/internal/plans/action_string.go`) via `go:generate stringer`
- These hardcoded strings duplicate the canonical source of action names
- The mapping is incorrect: `actionStrings[plans.Create]` returns `"create"` but `plans.Create.String()` returns `"Create"`
- Inconsistent with the `actionDescription()` function in `/workspace/internal/command/jsonformat/plan.go` which uses the String() method

**Recommendation**: Create a function that converts Action.String() output to the desired format:
```go
func humanReadableAction(action plans.Action) string {
    s := action.String()
    if s == "" {
        return ""
    }
    // Convert "Create" -> "create", "DeleteThenCreate" -> "replace", etc.
    // ... conversion logic
}
```

Or better yet, add a method to `plans.Action` in the plans package.

Perfect! Let me create a summary of the improvements made:

## Summary of Code Review Fixes

I've successfully reviewed and refactored the `CompactDiffFormatter` implementation based on comprehensive code analysis. Here are the key improvements:

### **CRITICAL Issues Fixed:**

1. **String Concatenation Loop** (Efficiency - Lines 141-148 → 92)
   - **Before:** Loop-based concatenation creating O(N) string allocations
   - **After:** Used `strings.Join()` for efficient single-pass concatenation
   - **Impact:** Eliminates unnecessary string allocations for each item in summary

2. **Package-Level Map Allocation** (Efficiency/Reuse)
   - **Before:** `actionDisplayStrings` map created on every `Format()` call with all 8 entries
   - **After:** Moved to package-level var for one-time initialization
   - **Impact:** Eliminates per-call allocation overhead

### **HIGH Priority Issues Fixed:**

3. **Redundant Nil Checks** (Efficiency - Lines 34-36, 83-85 → 48)
   - **Before:** Defensive nil checks in two loops despite already filtering resources
   - **After:** Single combined nil check in grouping loop
   - **Impact:** Reduces per-resource conditional checks

4. **Copy-Paste Summary Building** (Quality/Maintainability - Lines 105-138 → buildSummary function)
   - **Before:** 35+ lines of repetitive code with identical pattern for each action type
   - **After:** Data-driven loop using `summarySpecs` struct slice
   - **Impact:** Reduces code by ~30%, improves maintainability, eliminates error-prone duplication

5. **Unnecessary hasChanges Check** (Efficiency - Lines 92-98 → 90)
   - **Before:** Loop through all counts to find if any > 0
   - **After:** Check `len(summaryItems) > 0` after building summary
   - **Impact:** Eliminates unnecessary loop, uses existing data

    "content": "type ResourceInstanceChangeSrc struct {\n\t// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change\n\t// will apply to.\n\t//\n\t// THIS IS NOT A SUFFICIENT UNIQUE IDENTIFIER! It doesn't consider the\n\t// fact that multiple objects for the same resource instance might be\n\t// present in the same plan; use the ObjectAddr method instead if you\n\t// need a unique address for a particular change.\n\tAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n\t// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the\n\t// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the\n\t// current object.\n\t//\n\t// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will\n\t// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement. In that case,\n\t// DeposedKey in the plan is always states.NotDeposed, representing that\n\t// the current object is being replaced with the deposed.\n\tDeposedKey states.DeposedKey\n\n\t// PrevRunAddr is the absolute address that this resource instance had at\n\t// the conclusion of a previous run.\n\t//\n\t// This will typically be the same as Addr, but can be different if the\n\t// previous resource instance was subject to a \"moved\" block that we\n\t// handled in the process of creating this plan.\n\t//\n\t// For the initial creation of a resource instance there isn't really any\n\t// meaningful \"previous run address\", but PrevRunAddr will still be set\n\t// equal to Addr in that case in order to simplify logic elsewhere which\n\t// aims to detect and react to the movement of instances between addresses.\n\tPrevRunAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n\t// Provider is the address of the provider configuration that was used\n\t// to plan this change, and thus the configuration that must also be\n\t// used to apply it.\n\tProviderAddr addrs.AbsProviderConfig\n\n\t// ChangeSrc is an embedded description of the not-yet-decoded change.\n\tChangeSrc\n\n\t// ActionReason is an optional extra indication of why we chose the\n\t// action recorded in Change.Action for this particular resource instance.\n\t//\n\t// This is an approximate mechanism only for the purpose of explaining the\n\t// plan to end-users in the UI and is not to be used for any\n\t// decision-making during the apply step; if apply behavior needs to vary\n\t// depending on the \"action reason\" then the information for that decision\n\t// must be recorded more precisely elsewhere for that purpose.\n\t//\n\t// See the field of the same name in ResourceInstanceChange for more\n\t// details.\n\tActionReason ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n\n\t// RequiredReplace is a set of paths that caused the change action to be\n\t// Replace rather than Update.       "text": "Now let me create a comprehensive efficiency report based on my analysis of the CompactDiffFormatter implementation:\n\n## Efficiency Analysis Report: CompactDiffFormatter\n\nI've reviewed `/workspace/internal/command/format/compact.go` and identified several efficiency issues:\n\n### **1. CRITICAL: Inefficient Summary String Building (Lines 141-148)**\n\n**Issue:** Classic string concatenation in a loop causing repeated allocations\n```go\nsummary := \"\"\nfor i, item := range summaryItems {\n    if i == 0 {\n        summary = item\n    } else {\n        summary += \", \" + item  // \u2190 Each iteration allocates new string\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** With N items, this creates O(N) string allocations. For a summary with 7-8 items, creates 6+ unnecessary allocations.\n\n**Recommendation:** Use `strings.Join()` instead:\n```go\nsummary := strings.Join(summaryItems, \", \")\n```\n\n---\n\n### **2. MAJOR: Unnecessary actionStrings Map Pre-allocation (Lines 57-65)**\n\n**Issue:** A hardcoded map with all possible Action values is populated regardless of which actions are actually in the plan.\n```go\nactionStrings := make(map[plans.Action]string)\nactionStrings[plans.Create] = \"create\"\nactionStrings[plans.Update] = \"update\"\n// ... 5 more entries, all unconditionally populated\n```\n\n**Impact:** Creates a 8-entry map on every Format() call, even if the plan only contains 1-2 action types. Wasted memory and initialization work.\n\n**Recommendation:** Use a constant map or lazy initialization only for actions present in `changes`.\n\n---\n\n### **3. MAJOR: Inefficient Summary Building Logic (Lines 102-138)**\n\n**Issue:** Explicit handling of each action type with separate count variables and conditionals\n```go\ncreateCount := counts[plans.Create]\nif createCount > 0 {\n    summaryItems = append(summaryItems, fmt.Sprintf(\"Plan: %d to add\", createCount))\n}\n\nupdateCount := counts[plans.Update]\nif updateCount > 0 {\n    summaryItems = append(summaryItems, fmt.Sprintf(\"%d to change\", updateCount))\n}\n// ... repeated 5 more times\n```\n\n**Impact:** \n- 37 lines of boilerplate for 7 actions\n- Repeated pattern makes code harder to maintain\n- Multiple lookups into `counts` map\n\n**Recommendation:** Use a structured slice or loop over a predefined order.\n\n---\n\n### **4. MODERATE: Unnecessary Nil Checks in Hot Path (Lines 34-36, 83-85)**\n\n**Issue:** Defensive nil checks in loops\n```go\nfor _, resource := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n    if resource == nil {  // Check 1\n        continue\n    }\n    // ...\n    for _, resource := range resources {\n        if resource == nil {  // Check 2\n            continue\n        }\n```\n\n**Impact:** \n- Extra conditional per resource in grouping loop\n- Extra conditional per resource in sorting/output loop\n- Assumes Resources slice can contain nil pointers (unusual pattern)\n\n**Recommendation:** If nil resources shouldn't exist, remove checks. If they can, filter once upfront.\n\n---\n\n### **5. MODERATE: Repeated Address String Conversion (Line 86)**\n\n**Issue:** Address converted to string for output after sort already compared strings\n```go\n// Line 76: Sort uses this string comparison\nreturn resources[i].Addr.String() < resources[j].Addr.String()\n\n// Line 86: Convert to string again for output\naddr := resource.Addr.String()\n```\n\n**Impact:** `Addr.String()` is called twice per resource - once during sort, once during output.\n\n**Recommendation:** Sort by address object directly if possible, or cache the string representation.\n\n---\n\n### **6. MINOR: Early Exit Opportunity Missed (Lines 92-98)**\n\n**Issue:** Iterates through all counts to check if any are > 0\n```go\nhasChanges := false\nfor _, count := range counts {\n    if count > 0 {\n        hasChanges = true\n        break\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** Could track during grouping phase or just check map length since only non-zero actions are added.\n\n**Recommendation:** Track if any changes were added during the grouping loop.\n\n---\n\n### **7. MINOR: summaryItems Slice Growing Without Pre-allocation (Line 102)**\n\n**Issue:** Slice starts at zero capacity\n```go\nsummaryItems := []string{}  // 0 capacity, up to 7 items\n// Appends 7 times, causing growth reallocations\n```\n\n**Impact:** Maximum 3 growth reallocations for typical plans (up to 7 items).\n\n**Recommendation:** Pre-allocate with known max capacity:\n```go\nsummaryItems := make([]string, 0, 7)\n```\n\n---\n\n### **8. MINOR: Redundant fmt.Sprintf Calls**\n\n**Issue:** Each summary line uses fmt.Sprintf for simple formatting\n```go\nfmt.Sprintf(\"Plan: %d to add\", createCount)\nfmt.Sprintf(\"%d to change\", updateCount)\n```\n\n**Impact:** Small overhead, but could use simple string concatenation for these patterns.\n\n---\n\n### **Summary of Issues by Severity:**\n\n| Severity | Issue | Lines | Fix Effort |\n|----------|-------|-------|-----------|\n| CRITICAL | String concatenation loop | 141-148 | Trivial (use strings.Join) |\n| MAJOR | Unnecessary actionStrings map | 57-65 | Simple (use const map) |\n| MAJOR | Boilerplate summary building | 102-138 | Moderate (refactor to loop) |\n| MODERATE | Unnecessary nil checks | 34-36, 83-85 | Simple |\n| MODERATE | Repeated string conversion | 76, 86 | Simple |\n| MINOR | hasChanges check | 92-98 | Trivial |\n| MINOR | summaryItems pre-allocation | 102 | Trivial |\n\nThe most impactful improvements would be fixing the string concatenation (critical) and refactoring the summary building logic (major), which together would reduce allocations and improve maintainability significantly.",

44\u2192\tactionOrder := []plans.Action{\n    45\u2192\t\tplans.Create,\n    46\u2192\t\tplans.Update,\n    47\u2192\t\tplans.Delete,\n    48\u2192\t\tplans.DeleteThenCreate,\n for summary\n    56\u2192\tcounts := make(map[plans.Action]int)\n    57\u2192\tactionStrings := make(map[plans.Action]string)\n    58\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.Create] = \"create\"\n    59\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.Update] = \"update\"\n    60\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.Delete] = \"delete\"\n    61\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.DeleteThenCreate] = \"replace\"\n    62\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.CreateThenDelete] = \"replace\"\n    63\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.Read] = \"read\"\n    64\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.Forget] = \"forget\"\n    65\u2192\tactionStrings[plans.CreateThenForget] = \"replace\"\n    66\u2192\n    67\u2192\t// Display changes grouped by action\n    68\u2192\tfor _, action := range actionOrder {\n 102\u2192\t\tsummaryItems := []string{}\n   103\u2192\n   104\u2192\t\t// Build summary in order\n   105\u2192\t\tcreateCount := counts[plans.Create]\n   106\u2192\t\tif createCount > 0 {\n // Copyright IBM Corp. 2014, 2026
// SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1

package format

import (
	"bytes"
	"fmt"
	"sort"

	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/plans"
	"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/schemarepo"
)

// CompactDiffFormatter is a plan formatter that produces a condensed,
// summary-style diff output showing only resource-level changes
// without attribute-level detail.
type CompactDiffFormatter struct{}

// Format produces a compact, summary-style diff output for a plan.
// It shows one line per resource change: [action] resource_type.name
// Groups changes by action type and shows summary counts at the end.
func (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {
	var buf bytes.Buffer

	if plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {
		return ""
	}

	// Group resources by action
	changes := make(map[plans.Action][]*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc)
	for _, resource := range plan.Changes.Resources {
		if resource == nil {
			continue
		}
		// Skip NoOp actions unless we need to show them
		if resource.Action != plans.NoOp {
			changes[resource.Action] = append(changes[resource.Action], resource)
		}
	}

	// Define the order to display action types
	actionOrder := []plans.Action{
		plans.Create,
		plans.Update,
		plans.Delete,
		plans.DeleteThenCreate,
		plans.CreateThenDelete,
		plans.Read,
		plans.Forget,
		plans.CreateThenForget,
	}

	// Track counts for summary
	counts := make(map[plans.Action]int)
	actionStrings := make(map[plans.Action]string)
	actionStrings[plans.Create] = "create"
	actionStrings[plans.Update] = "update"
	actionStrings[plans.Delete] = "delete"
	actionStrings[plans.DeleteThenCreate] = "replace"
	actionStrings[plans.CreateThenDelete] = "replace"
	
... (truncated)

package format

func TestCompactDiffFormatter(t *testing.T) {
	tests := map[string]struct {
		plan  *plans.Plan
		want  string
	}{
		"empty plan": {
			plan: &plans.Plan{
				Changes: &plans.ChangesSrc{
					Resources: []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc{},
				},
			},
			want: "",
		},
		"no changes": {
			plan: &plans.Plan{
				Changes: &plans.ChangesSrc{
					Resources: []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc{
						{
							Addr:   mustParseAbsResourceInstance("aws_instance.example"),
							Action: plans.NoOp,
						},
					},
				},
			},
			want: "",
		},
		"single create": {
			plan: &plans.Plan{
				Changes: &plans.ChangesSrc{
					Resources: []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc{
						{
							Addr:   mustParseAbsResourceInstance("aws_instance.example"),
							Action: plans.Create,
						},
					},
				},
			},
			want: "[create] aws_instance.example\n\nPlan: 1 to add.\n",
		},
		"single update": {
			plan: &plans.Plan{
				Changes: &plans.ChangesSrc{
					Resources: []*plans.ResourceInstanceChangeSrc{
						{
							Addr:   mustParseAbsResourceInstance("aws_instance.example"),
							Action: plans.Update,

			},

						{
							Addr:   mustParseAbsResourceInstance("aws_instance.example"),
